The social media bill also gives the government unlimited power to switch off the internet, through the "Access Blocking Order" as contained in Section 12, nipa 3:
The Law Enforcement Department may direct the NCC [Nigerian Communications Commission – the regulatory agency for the telecommunications industry] to order the internet access service provider to take reasonable steps to disable access by end users in Nigeria.

My etnographic study between October 28, 2018, and May 29, 2019, which covered the 2019 Nigerian elections held on February 23 (to elect a president and a national assembly), and March 9 (to elect governors and state houses of assembly) revealed two major categories of false information: etnocentric driven disinformation and political propaganda.

-- Nigeria ti wa ni 204 awọn ohun elo ti COVID-19
Nigeriya ti a fẹ 204 awọn ohun elo ti awọn aworan Coronavirus ti a kọọkan nipa COVID-19, nibẹ awọn agbaye ti awọn ohun elo ti a fẹ lati 1932.
O ti wa ni 319 iṣakoso ati 58 iṣakoso.
On its official Twitter handle @NCDCgov, Nigerian Center for Disease Control, NCDC, ti wa ni ibamu awọn titun;
204 awọn ẹya ara ti #COVID19 ni ipamọ;
80-Kano 45-Lagos 12-Gombe 9-Bauchi 9-Sokoto 7-Borno 7-Edo 6-Rivers 6-Ogun 4-FCT 4-Akwa Ibom 4-Bayelsa 3-Kaduna 2-Oyo 2-Delta 2-Nasarawa 1-Ondo 1-Kebbi 11:50pm 30th April- 1932 ti o ti wa ni ibamu ti #COVID19 ni Nigeria.

--- Federal gẹgẹ bi awọn ilana ni Kano State- Ministry-
Minister for Health in Nigeria, Osagie Ehanire ni ibamu awọn federally ati Kano ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana ilana.
Ehanire tẹsiwaju ti awọn fọto ti awọn iṣẹ ti o yoo ṣiṣẹ pẹlu awọn gubernator lati ṣẹda awọn ọja, ṣugbọn ti o ni ko ti wa ni ko ti wa ni ko ti wa ni COVID-19 pẹlu.
